Shen Bao National Goods Weekly

National Goods Forum

Shameless Behavior 277

— Natural

A London dispatch dated the 30th of last month reported that Japan's unfair competition methods have provoked vehement attacks in the British House of Commons. A high-ranking official of the Board of Trade, Mr. Runciman, delivered a speech in the House, expressing great indignation at Japanese goods being passed off as British goods and using British trademarks. Mr. Runciman stated that governments of all countries should actively take measures to suppress such shameless behavior. Therefore, the British government, after obtaining concrete evidence, should lodge a formal protest with the Japanese government without regard for diplomatic niceties.

When our countrymen read this news item, what thoughts arise if they close their eyes and reflect? The Japanese have been engaging in shameless behavior towards our country for more than just a day. They clearly come from Japan but are labeled as made in Germany, the United States, or other countries. They are clearly Japanese goods but falsely claim to be domestic products. While discerning people can easily see through such tricks, many of our countrymen are regrettably deceived. This counterfeit branding alone deprives our domestic goods of considerable sales each year. However, this reporter believes that we should not blame others for such shameless behavior but first blame ourselves. It is only because there are shameless countrymen that the Japanese dare to engage in such shameless tricks. In the entire country, there are many people who act as accomplices to tigers, blinded by greed. To call them shameless countrymen is a mild term. Does the reader doubt my words? They clearly purchase Japanese yarn but claim it is domestic. They clearly purchase Japanese cloth but falsely claim they wove it themselves. They use their skills of deception to secretly alter appearances in the dark of night. People's lack of conscience has reached such a point. Yet, they still call themselves merchants in society and remain nonchalant. They use domestic brand names to sell Japanese goods and remain nonchalant. They install a few machines to put on a show and secretly smuggle in goods, remaining nonchalant. People say that the most degenerate people in the country are those in Shanghai. This is because the people of Shanghai are too focused on profit, disregarding everything else. Mr. Hu'e Sheng said, "People today have increasingly thick skin, and their masks cannot be torn off unless they are directly punished in person." These words keenly capture the psychology of Shanghai society. As a reporter, I know that speaking these words will offend people, but driven by my conscience, I must speak them. I hope that readers will:

(1) From now on, pay attention to this shameless behavior and no longer be deceived by it.

(2) From now on, abandon sentimentality. If any of your relatives or friends engage in this shameless behavior, you should sincerely advise and scold them face-to-face. If they refuse to listen to your scolding, sever ties with them and reject them together. Expel them to the four barbarian lands, not associating with them in China. I would also like to offer a final piece of sincere advice to those who still want to engage in selling inferior goods: There are many occupations in the world, and many businesses can be operated for profit. Why sacrifice your conscience, defy the world's condemnation, and engage in this risky, opportunistic behavior that harms others and damages the country? Lay down the butcher knife and become a Buddha on the spot. In human society, life is at most a hundred years. It is better to do more things that you can be proud of, becoming an upright and honest person.

Discussion on National Goods

After Reading "How Should We Promote National Goods in the Countryside?" 278

— Zhang Mengzhao

After reading Mr. Huang Yingdai's article "How Should We Promote National Goods in the Countryside" in this publication, I feel that what Mr. Huang said is indeed to the point, but I have some supplementary opinions "regarding how to promote national goods in the countryside," which I write below.

This summer, I happened to travel to Jiaoshan Township in Wuxi because of something. Those so-called sacred farmers and farm women there mostly admire new Shanghai decorations and new patterns, constantly praising them in their mouths. There is a wealthy household in the township that has a radio and a phonograph. After finishing their work in the fields, they run to listen to it with great joy, gathering a large crowd. When they hear a very beautiful tune, they also hum along. Therefore, it is not necessary to preach in the countryside, because to preach effectively in the field, one must become a farmer and join their ranks to promote national goods. Otherwise, lecturing in a serious and pretentious manner will definitely not be effective. We may as well use the all-powerful radio to instill national goods news and songs into their minds. It is also easy for rural cooperatives to set up one. Although there is no substitute national product for the radio yet, it is more worthwhile to prevent the dumping of a large number of Western goods and the alarming outflow of interests with one radio. The Japanese, who have the most solid patriotism, the government still announced that there are dozens of non-national products that they cannot create themselves and have to use. Second: Celebrities who promote national products should discuss with the domestic film company authorities to shoot more "plays that show the pain of foreign goods oppression and the joy of people using national goods to save the country." They should come to the inland countryside to screen them. In the countryside without electricity, they should cooperate with vigilant paintings to issue a kind of daily national goods voucher. If the villagers want money, they can take money; if they want to buy some daily necessities, they can take some "daily national goods vouchers." If we work hard to promote in this way and implement it in a planned way, I believe that national goods will definitely sweep away imported goods in the countryside, and everyone will happily use national goods! What do you readers think?

The National Goods Movement and Rural Relief 279

— Fang Cuinong

- Dedicated to those who promote national goods and serve rural businesses -

We all know that China is based on the countryside. Undoubtedly, the promotion of national goods should also focus on the vast countryside. Moreover, we all know that the biggest reason for the bankruptcy of the rural economy is the invasion of foreign economies, and isn't economic invasion caused by the filling of the market with foreign goods; so that farmers also abandon local goods to buy foreign goods?

As long as we open our eyes, we can see everywhere in the countryside that farmers also use foreign goods, such as kerosene and cigarettes that occupy most of the small shops and stalls... Rural women also mostly wear foreign goods such as printed foreign yarn and flannel... In short, the countryside has obviously gone bankrupt now, but they still wear foreign cloth, use foreign goods, and even eat foreign rice... This kind of bleak phenomenon should not have happened after the National Goods Year of 1933 - and it should not be discovered again under the revival of the countryside - I think that the current promotion of national goods to relieve the countryside should be carried out in two ways.

The first is to promote the use of national goods by farmers; because rural people lack knowledge, have no national concept, and are selfish and greedy for immediate small profits; so they are easily fooled by merchants to purchase foreign goods. In addition, there is a lack of opportunities to buy national goods in the countryside. - So promoting national goods is also very important, but whether in the countryside or the city, advertising and promotion are very ineffective. I think it is necessary to promote it in the countryside

How Exactly Is China Contributing as One of Twenty-Seven Nations? 280

— Yang Mang

It's a pity that the empty show of resistance is gaining momentum, and Japanese goods are flooding in like a tide. According to a survey by the Trade Bureau of the Japanese Ministry of Commerce and Industry on November 30, the prevention of imports of Japanese goods by various countries around the world is now becoming more intense, reaching as many as twenty-seven countries. The preventive measures are all policies such as raising tariffs, import permits, exchange controls, and dumping taxes. From this point of view, there are actually twenty-seven countries in the world that are resisting Japanese goods, and poor China actually accounts for one of the twenty-seven countries. However, in fact, China's resistance to Japanese goods is probably just writing a few articles, holding a few meetings, and drafting a few regulations, and then it's over. Has there ever been a real preparation, a whole plan, and a sincere and determined effort to work quickly, practically, and hard? After reading this news, the reporter felt really ashamed and sad. This year was wasted as a National Goods Year, but unexpectedly created an opportunity for Japanese goods to sell well. Do readers also know that Japanese goods are everywhere in North China? Do they also know that Japanese goods are smuggled everywhere in the Shanghai market? Do they also know that Japanese goods are active everywhere in the ports along the Yangtze River? Others have built solid defenses, marched swiftly, and have achieved results in resisting Japanese goods. We are putting on an empty show, with only outward appearances. As a result, the more we advocate resistance, the more rampant Japanese goods become. This newspaper published on the 5th that the International Trade Bureau released the prices of imported cosmetics and perfumes from various countries from January to October this year, reaching 1,398,664 yuan. In addition to the United States, France, and Britain, Japan is the most. As the Japanese Daily reported, Japan shipped more than 21,000 pieces of fresh and salted Japanese fish from Qingdao and Dalian last week, with a total value of more than 500,000 yuan. May I ask, is this resisting Japanese goods? Or is it promoting the sale of Japanese goods? The phenomenon is like this, which is lamentable. If European countries feel that Japanese goods are being dumped, they either loudly call for attention or actively defend against and restrict them. Italian Prime Minister Mussolini, witnessing the monopoly of the Asian market by Japanese cotton textiles and the invasion of Italy by Far Eastern rayon, has long been in contact with Germany and Russia to find ways to resist. Looking at our country, government officials are busy with civil wars, and social industries and commerce are too busy to save themselves. As a result, the Japanese lure from the outside, and good merchants collude from the inside, and such a large China has become a large market for Japanese goods to be active. Every time I think about it, I feel heartbroken. Recently, Mr. Zhang Gongquan, after inspecting the Northwest, talked about the localism of Shanxi people, which is even more than patriotism. The only purpose of Shanxi people buying goods is to use self-sufficient Shanxi goods. If it is not enough, they use Chinese goods. If it is not enough, they use imported goods. Everything must be subject to the Economic Control Bureau. Even with cigarettes, the issuance of licenses is very strict. Merchants who have licenses are only allowed to sell Shanxi cigarettes. Shanghai cigarettes and British and American cigarettes are not easy to obtain. The strictness of the defenses can be seen. In my opinion, although the method of Shanxi people is limited to regional views, their courage to resist foreign goods is admirable. Secondly, the industrial control in Guangxi Province adheres to the policy that imports must not exceed exports, and its courage is also commendable. If Chinese people can all be like this, and all places can be like this, then there is no need to talk about resisting Japanese goods, and Japanese goods will have no way to enter. Otherwise, being listed as one of the twenty-seven countries, and having an empty name for resisting Japanese goods, the future of the national goods industry will be even more unbearable to hear.

In order to promote national goods, the following points should be noted:

1. There should be young men and women who "lead by example" to guide farmers to happily use national goods.

2. Use a roving national goods exhibition to collect various national goods needed by farmers and exhibit them in the countryside after the autumn harvest.

3. Show slide shows and movies about national goods... to arouse interest in buying national goods.

4. Set up a small-scale national goods specimen exhibition room in the local agricultural education center, primary school, or improvement association to enable farmers to recognize national goods.

5. Manufacturers should negotiate with local cooperatives to wholesale or lend to farmers.

6. Wholesale to peddlers so that they can sell in the countryside.

The second is to use the original production in the countryside to supplement the lack of national goods. We know that in the past, the countryside has always been that men farmed and women weaved, without seeking external forces. They wore native cloth, used native goods, lit lamps with rapeseed oil and vegetable oil, made clothes with self-woven native cloth, and smoked self-grown native tobacco... Therefore, in addition to promoting national goods, we should use the original production to improve it to remedy the lack of national goods and economic losses. We should also cooperate with manufacturers to use the low wages of rural women to do handicrafts (such as pasting matchboxes), and promote the cultivation of pyrethrum, mint, daylilies, cotton... to subsidize the raw materials for manufacturing national goods and increase the income from rural production. It will also be of great benefit to promoting national goods to relieve the countryside.

In short, in China, where the rural economy has gone bankrupt and the market is filled with foreign goods, to promote national goods. I think the above two points are indeed things that cannot be ignored; moreover, national goods and the countryside have a close relationship. It can be said that national goods completely rely on the countryside, whether it is its raw materials or sales channels, the countryside must be the main base. - In the past, the reason why national goods could not be developed was also largely related to the fact that the movement was focused only on cities! From now on, promoting national goods and relieving the countryside should work together to plan. In other words: manufacturers and rural service personnel should be in close contact: so that the supply of raw materials for national goods and the sales channels of products can be adjusted!

Finally! I hope that comrades who promote national goods and relieve the countryside will pay attention to it; and give me some correction -

Discussion on National Goods

Promoting National Goods Should Start with Oneself 281

— Ling Bai

It seems a bit excessive, but I dare to state responsibly that this is absolutely true.

This place is the highest authority for national administration and academic research. Therefore, the middle and senior staff here are all first-class scholars and patriots in the country. Even general assistants and trainees, etc., are all gilded with a layer of gold—Bachelor’s degrees.

The matters we research are said to be: (1) how to develop the national economy, (2) how to revive the countryside, (3) how to increase the production of national goods, (4) how to resist the import of foreign goods, and (5) how to enrich the people's strength, (6) how to improve the people's livelihood... and other issues of "national economy and people's livelihood."

However, unfortunately! Our rural people have long been working hard, digging up their labor and squeezing dry their sweat and blood. Even more unfortunately, what they get in return for their hard work throughout the year is clothes that cannot cover their bodies and food that cannot fill their stomachs. Even the lowest standard of living is difficult to maintain. Without sufficient production funds and without adequate living materials, they eat rural brown rice, wear rural native cloth, and use rural handicraft products. They have no better purchasing power or consumption power. How can they increase production? They have long been eating national goods and using national goods.

Only citizens' meetings are the target of our national goods movement.

But in this highest authority for national administration and academic research, many young scholars and patriots serve in national public institutions, earn taxes from the blood and sweat of the people, research the national economy and people's livelihood, and talk and write about saving the country, but how contradictory are the facts! They! Eighty-eight percent of them wear brand-new and smart foreign-made suits, live in tall foreign buildings of cement and steel, eat coffee, bread, whiskey, and brandy, and use Western-style furniture and decorations. They occupy the upper layer of society, have great purchasing power and consumption power, but they have forgotten that "everyone is responsible for the rise and fall of the country"!

Is there anything surprising about this? Aren't all the facts presented in our society so common and prevalent? Is there anything special about this place! But to talk about saving the country, to talk about reviving the countryside, and to develop the national economy, we must first promote national goods and engage in the national goods movement. This is the duty of every compatriot and also the responsibility of every compatriot.

- Alas! The national crisis is pressing, I hope our compatriots will be more vigilant! Don't forget that "promoting national goods should start with oneself." - This is our only creed.

Merchants Promoting National Goods in the Countryside 282

— Que Baling

In the last two issues of this publication, there were articles about "promoting national goods in the countryside," which made me have endless feelings.

What I mean by feelings is not that national goods should not be promoted in the countryside. Strictly speaking, the enemy of national goods is not in the countryside, but in the cities, not in the hard-working farmers, but in the general intellectual class who call themselves modern. This is not an exaggeration, but there are facts to prove it.

My relative, Mr. X (farmer), when his children (I won't mention their names) were studying in the countryside, all their clothes were completely native cloth. When they grew up and went to study in the city, all their clothes and supplies hated native goods and admired foreign goods. Every year the cost is quite high. Mr. X occasionally mentioned this, and there must be endless emotions in it.

The above is not a deliberate fabrication, but an absolutely true fact. The reason why I want to present it in this publication is to prove that the focus of promoting national goods is 30% in the countryside and 70% still in the prosperous cities and the intellectual class.

Therefore, I believe that while promoting national goods, the countryside should not be abandoned, but the city should not be taken lightly. It should be known that those who wear foreign goods and use foreign objects are generally modern people, and there are few simple rural people. I think everyone will agree with this.

In summary, to sum it up in one sentence, the promotion of national goods requires the concerted efforts of the whole country, both urban and rural, A part of the promotion and the efforts of one place still do not have much effect.

Special Discussion on National Goods

The Various Aspects of Housewives Promoting National Goods 284

— Yu Sisi

The National Goods Exhibition organized by the Young Women's Christian Association is about to open. As Mr. Yang An said, whether the promotion of national goods is successful or not depends on the hands of the ladies and wives. The reason why the past national goods movement failed was because the promoters did not pay attention to the ladies and wives. Now, the Young Women's Christian Association, with the grandmothers and wives as the backbone, is automatically rising up to hold a national goods exhibition, which is such a gratifying thing. The goods they are exhibiting are aimed at families, and they are divided into three grades according to the economic situation of general families, which is very novel and meets the needs of reality. Housewives who have never used national goods or do not know what national goods are, if they visit, will definitely have a clear understanding of national goods. They must not forget after the visit, and they should use national goods forever from now on. But, how should housewives promote national goods? Although the exhibition has already displayed many national goods of different categories, which can be used as a reference for the ladies and wives, I think there are still a few points that are also worth paying attention to by the ladies and wives.

Restraining Husbands

No one can deny that the most powerful force in restraining men is their wives. Men often act blindly based on their own will, and it is difficult for others to persuade him to change his mind. Only a beloved wife can find a way to make him change his mind. Many men are enthusiastic about imported goods. Those who are his wives should exert her mission, work hard to restrain him and persuade him, and not allow him to buy a single foreign product. It is best to throw a tantrum at him when he buys foreign goods and returns, and give him the "cold shoulder." As a result of this non-cooperation, he will not buy those "damn" imported goods again next time. Mr. Yang An said: If the husband buys foreign goods, the wife can implement a strike or file for divorce. This is the best method.

Advising Children

Housewives have more opportunities to contact their children, and they have the most influence on them. If housewives use national goods, the children will naturally hate foreign goods after being impressed for a long time. Otherwise, innocent children will also like to use foreign goods, which will have an infinite impact on the future of national goods. Therefore, a virtuous mother must often advise her children on the meaning of promoting national goods, so that a concept of national goods remains in their innocent souls: at the same time, she must of course use national goods for the goods she consumes, and set an example.

Restraining Servants

Servants have very little knowledge and simple minds. They simply do not know what it means to love the country and use national goods. When the master orders them to buy things, they often buy foreign goods. Therefore, housewives should often restrain them and guide them to buy national goods.

Recognizing National Goods

There is also one point that is very important, and that is that housewives should pay more attention to recognizing national goods. Because now unscrupulous merchants know that it is difficult to sell enemy goods, they often change the appearance of foreign goods and pretend to be national goods. The techniques they use are clever and powerful. Housewives who are enthusiastic about national goods may accidentally buy these things, which would be too disappointing for their sincerity in promoting and loving the country. Therefore, housewives must carefully remember the trademarks, brands, and factory names of national goods products in order to avoid being deceived by unscrupulous merchants.

Miscellaneous Talk on National Goods

Where to Start Promoting National Goods 285

— He Bi

Promoting national goods, "start with children": This is what many people are saying, and many people are also agreeing with it; but how should we do it? The answer is this, saying, we should ask parents to pay attention and not give children anything other than national goods, and parents themselves should never use foreign goods, setting an example so that children have a mentality of loving national goods and hating enemy goods. Then this responsibility is entirely on the parents, and the burden of promoting national goods rests on the parents first.

Another saying is that to promote national goods "start with elementary school teachers", because one elementary school teacher is in contact with many children, and is also a standard for children. Many, many children follow their teachers in using national goods, so the application of national goods is considerable! These points are indeed the great way to promote national goods.

However, on the other hand, we must also hope for creation, because we ask national goods to replace foreign goods completely, so that everything that everyone's eyes come into contact with is national goods, then there is no need to check, all goods are domestic products, it is easy to adopt, and the elimination of national goods is also good. - Because sometimes there is still the suffering of buying the wrong thing? At present, the results of compatriots using national goods are much higher than before. If you don't believe it, you only need to go to the national goods market on Nanjing Road to prove it. So I say that to promote national goods "start with creating national goods". In addition, "national goods are on sale" is also an excellent method.

From what has been said above, as long as national goods can be equal to foreign goods, and national goods are not more expensive than foreign goods, then soon everyone will use national goods, and national goods will be consumed by the people. This year's National Goods Year will also be worthy of its name.

Finally, I calculated that there is only a whole month left in the National Goods Year. After January, it will be the first National Goods Year, but I hope that national goods manufacturers will continue to create and continue to promote sales.

Contributing Opinions

On the Art of Advertising Domestic Goods 286

— Quan Jia

To revitalize domestic goods, advertising is indeed a necessary tool. However, in the initial stages of promoting domestic goods, how should advertising be made more practical? Now, I offer several suggestions for the domestic goods industry.

(1) It is often seen that during a major sale at domestic goods companies, advertising papers are plastered all over the walls. This actually makes people pay less attention. Moreover, it is a waste of paper and does not help. I suggest sticking to designated advertising columns, or using the remaining money to buy domestic goods and offer them as prizes for essay contests, awarding prizes to the best entries. Wouldn't that kill two birds with one stone?

(2) Regarding advertisements for domestic goods companies, I believe it's better to explain their true strengths and weaknesses and compare them with foreign goods, rather than simply saying how good they are, or even saying they are no different from foreign goods. The former is nothing more than deception, while the latter increases genuine sympathy from the Chinese people.

(3) In addition, it is best to focus advertising slightly more on the inland areas, because the tentacles of imperialism have reached into the inland, and what the people see and hear is nothing more than foreign propaganda. Therefore, for the majority of the people to know about domestic goods, this is the most important condition. The establishment of domestic goods companies in various regions by the China Production and Sales Cooperation Association is for this purpose.

Finally, the advertising techniques for our domestic goods business urgently need to be economical, effective, and rational. Otherwise, it is better to save the wasted money and focus on the quality of the products!

A Contribution to the Goods Manager of a Domestic Goods Factory 287

— Xu Nangong

In this year of promoting domestic goods, the mission of a domestic goods factory is not only to supply the commodities needed domestically, but also to be the vanguard in resisting foreign goods. Therefore, on the one hand, it is necessary to encourage the Chinese people to use domestic goods, and on the other hand, to strive for improvements in products and reductions in prices. However, in many factories at present, they temporarily seek profit while neglecting technological advancement, focusing on business development with a complacent mentality, or even engaging in cutthroat competition among themselves. I fear that before foreign goods can be completely resisted, the factories themselves will be shaken, leading to collapse, and the entire domestic goods business will be hindered as a result. The danger in the future is truly unimaginable!

Indeed, the main purpose of a factory is to develop its business, but if there are no good results in manufacturing, even if it is vigorously promoted and sells well for a time, failure is inevitable. Therefore, the quality of the products is also the key to future success or failure. This is an undeniable fact.

Since superior products are paramount, it is also necessary to manage goods perfectly. If a goods manager does not have a keen mind and accurate calculations, then errors in receiving and dispatching are unavoidable. For example, if a customer orders goods to be shipped to another location, and the manager, due to a moment's negligence, misallocates colors or quantities, and this is only discovered when the goods arrive at the other location, then the customer will sacrifice shipping costs and delay their business, and the factory's reputation will be damaged, leading to numerous disputes. The impact on the factory's reputation and business may be no less than the issue of product quality!

Therefore, the precision and thoroughness of a factory's goods manager in their duties is of great help to the progress of the business. In addition to the cleanliness of the goods storage, the accuracy of receiving and dispatching inspections, the speed of distribution and adjustment, and the solidity of packaging and assembly, they must also have a patient personality, an agile mind, and a hardworking spirit. This is the knowledge that every goods manager of a domestic goods factory should have!

Visit Notes: Visit to the China Nail Manufacturing Company 288

— Ji Yin Zhao

It is shameful to say that we in our country cannot even produce enough nails for our own needs, and must rely on imports, with large sums of money flowing abroad. This is such a shameful thing—last year's customs report: excluding those manufactured in factories set up in our country by foreigners, imports of round nails—commonly known as foreign nails—reached as many as 240,000 barrels (each barrel containing 100 pounds). Fellow countrymen, pay attention! Don't underestimate them just because a copper coin can buy several nails.

The China Nail Manufacturing Company was founded in November of the 20th year [of the Republic, i.e., 1931], and its rapid progress is unmatched by ordinary factories. It is of great value for visiting. I am a member of the industrial world, and I like to visit various factories. Hearing this news, I happily went to visit the factory on Funing Road in Yangshupu. Through the introduction of a friend and with the permission of the authorities, I followed the guide to the workshop. The machines roared, and the work was extremely tense. It was indeed a factory full of vitality. According to the guide, Manager Qian Xiangbiao studied in the United States for many years, specializing in machinery, and has a deep understanding of nail making. After returning, he organized this factory with his friend Ye Boyin and others. Through painstaking management, they have achieved this result.

In terms of equipment, there are currently sixteen nail-making machines, each of which can produce seventy or eighty barrels of round nails of various sizes in ten hours. The nails produced have the following advantages: "(1) The nail heads are round and even, with appropriate thickness: (2) The nail teeth are deep and firmly embedded: (3) The nail body is straight, unyielding, and unbending; (4) The nail tip is sharp and easily penetrates wood." In addition to nail making, there are also eight wire-drawing machines for drawing coarse wires into fine wires for nail making, thereby greatly reducing costs. There is a paper clip machine, so we will have domestic paper clips in the future, and we will no longer need to rely on imports. I heard that the China National Products Company is selling them for about ten cents per box. There is a barbed wire machine. It is said that the factory is currently actively expanding, and many other wire products will be launched one after another to meet the needs of society. After all, the factory's English name, Wire Product Co., is not limited to the manufacture of round nails.

In this year of promoting domestic goods, it is indeed worthy of praise to have such excellent domestic goods come into being, so I am happy to introduce them.

Notes on Visiting the China Industrial Machinery Manufacturing Factory 289

— Gan Chunquan

The China Industrial Machinery Manufacturing Factory is located at the intersection of Xiaoshadu Road and Macau Road in Shanghai. In terms of its history, it has always been part of the manufacturing department of the Commercial Press. In terms of its business scope, it specializes in manufacturing Shu-style Chinese typewriters. During this time, it went from Huadong Factory to Dadong Factory to Shiye Factory, undergoing several expansions and manufacturing. Recently, after the January 28th Incident, it was named the China Industrial Machinery Manufacturing Factory, with Mr. Song Mingde, the former director of the Chinese Typewriter Department of the Commercial Press, as the manager. Under Mr. Song's planning, the products have become more and more refined, and the business has become extremely prosperous. Now, by special contract with the Commercial Press, the manufacture of Chinese typewriters is the main product, and it also manufactures printing presses, instruments, stoves, desk calendars, and other products, which are also very popular in society. Yesterday, I received a special letter from Mr. Song, and the Shanghai Occupational Guidance Center sent me to visit. Those who went with me included Mr. Ni Baiyan, director of the China National Products Guidance Center. Now, I will write about what I saw during the visit to inform interested readers.

Chinese typewriters are related to cultural undertakings. They can replace writing, saving time and making reading easier. They have a wide range of applications. They were invented in the eighth year of the Republic of China [1919] by Mr. Shu Zhandong, and his contribution was great. Each machine has as many as 452 large and small parts. Because the parts are precision-made, the manufacturing is extremely serious. Most of the parts are manufactured by machines. If the parts made by the machines are deemed not accurate enough, they are transported to the fitter's department, where they are made very accurate and suitable for application by fine manual work. I will now describe the larger equipment of the factory that manufactures Chinese typewriters below.

(A) Lathe Department: This department has (1) small fine lathes, used for the more than 70 types of screws and perforated straight copper sheets; (2) universal large fine lathes, used for long-toothed parts with long grids and fixed plates with horizontal and vertical long teeth; (3) punch press, used for parts such as rolling drum walls and wall panels. There is also (4) an electric grinder for standby. (B) Fitter Department: This department is set up to use fine manual work to make the machine parts made by the lathe department very accurate when they are not accurate enough. All character pliers and grooved horizontal copper sheets in the character plate and various parts belong to this department. (C) Assembly Department: This department is specially set up for assembly after all the typewriters are made. Since a typewriter now has as many as 452 large and small parts, the assembly is done by skilled workers.

According to Manager Song, the factory can manufacture 15 Chinese typewriters per month, each worth 240 silver dollars. Currently, they are carefully studying to make the operation more responsive, reaching more than 1,200 words per hour, to facilitate the use of important documents such as official documents, letters, contracts, and agreements at any time. At the same time, they are trying to reduce costs so that all sectors can generally purchase them. Mr. Song's plan is of great benefit to the cultural sector. The other businesses of the factory, such as the production of printing presses, instruments, stoves, and desk calendars, are limited by space and cannot be fully described. Mr. Song welcomes visits from all sectors, and this is stated here.

Random Talk on Domestic Goods: Clothing, Food, Housing, and Transportation 292

— Yu Qiacheng

(1) Introduction

In our life process, we cannot go a day without clothing, food, housing, and transportation; however, these four aspects of people's livelihood in China have had several different periods. Looking back on the past and deciding on the future, we can only understand the phenomena of each period in detail and then choose what to take and what to discard!

(2) Before the Opening of the Maritime Ban

Clothing - homespun cloth

Food - domestic rice and wheat

Housing - all wood and bricks were made domestically

Transportation - boats and vehicles were all driven by Chinese people

Economic situation at that time: self-sufficient

(3) After the Opening of the Maritime Ban

Clothing - Adoration of foreign goods, homespun cloth was discarded

Food - Vegetables, rice and wheat were wholesale imported, Chinese tea was abandoned by Chinese people, and coffee was welcomed in China; even calculating candy, the leakage was enough to be shocking.

Housing - Building materials for Western-style houses, bricks, tiles, and foreign pine were mostly imported from abroad.

Transportation - The coal and gasoline for the power of boats and vehicles were mostly foreign products. Economic situation at that time: The people were poor and the country was exhausted.

(4) Current Transition Period

Clothing - Domestic silk and cloth have been improved, and the patterns and quality are not inferior to others.

Food - Sugar and sweets are mostly domestic products.

Housing - Brick and tile manufacturing also has factories run by Chinese people.

Transportation - ???

Current situation: National capital and foreign merchants are fighting.

(5) Future

Clothing, food, housing, and transportation, it all depends on how determined the Chinese people are. To be continued in the next episode.

National Goods Novel

New Cotton-Padded Jacket 293

— Hu Wen

It's getting cold, and the tattered cotton-padded jacket is still the one made five years ago. The wind drills in through the holes, like knives cutting the skin. It's really a bit too much! I've toughened my hide, so I can still bear it; but how can Ada, that little kid, be so thin-skinned and tender? A gust of wind comes, and he cries, shivering and whining. And my wife's heart always aches for the child, so she nags about it day and night.

Jin Sheng is really going to be driven to death!

No matter what, Ada has to have a new cotton-padded jacket made for him. My own cotton-padded jacket is too unsightly, and I have to get a new one too. Jin Sheng made up his mind, but where would the money come from? He had no choice but to discuss it with his wife and ask her relatives to borrow some money. Jin Sheng couldn't help but smile! He patted his rough, black hand on his pocket, and it was full of snow-white foreign coins!

The cloth was bought. A piece of flowery, colorful cloth for Ada's cotton-padded jacket, and a piece of black foreign cloth for himself. His wife took the flowery cloth, looked at it again and again, and then smiled with pursed lips. Jin Sheng also opened his big mouth and said triumphantly:

"Look! Is this cloth good or not? The price is also cheap! People say it's foreign goods, but who knows! What foreign goods, domestic goods, I don't understand at all! I only know to buy the one that's cheap!"

His wife praised his experience in buying cloth, which was even more abundant than a woman's, so Jin Sheng laughed again!

Wearing the new cotton-padded jacket, he felt the weather had become warmer. Ada also stopped crying.

Jin Sheng had to go to the mountains to collect firewood every day, and the thin branches broke his new cotton-padded jacket. Ada was playing with the little girl next door in the sun. The sun wasn't powerful, but it faded the color of Ada's flowery cotton-padded jacket.

His wife lost her temper and slammed the table, scolding:

"What's this! I borrowed money from the God of Wealth and worshiped the Bodhisattva to buy you these good foreign goods!"

How could foreign goods be so bad? Jin Sheng was really going to be driven to death!

— Yin Jiu

In front of a most modern three-dimensional building - a hostel, were parked new-style 1933 automobiles. The tall colorful archway obscured the original appearance and name of the hostel, undoubtedly making it known at a glance that this was a hall for holding a wedding ceremony. The endless stream of guests coming and going was enough to show that this "scene" was very grand.

After the wedding ceremony, the guests, especially the young people, forced the groom to report on his love story. The groom, Mr. Wang, was the winner of the National Language Speech Contest at ×× University, and of course began his report without any shyness:

Spring and Autumn

Circus 295

— Yang Yusheng

It is said that circuses are only for foreigners. This statement is probably discounted.

In China, everything likes to be "foreign," but there seem to be few people doing circuses. Even if there are, they are "rustic" and not worth watching!

The so-called circus, according to "reliable sources," is not entirely about horses performing; just as our Chinese monkey show is not entirely about monkeys performing. The latter, although not as beautiful as the former! There are rare birds and exotic animals, there are strongmen with bulging muscles, there are women with bare thighs; but pugs and sheep are indispensable! Sometimes, a bear can be brought out, which gives it a great circus style!

Circus and monkey show, judging from the words alone, can be sure that their content is different. However, both seem to need "people," especially circuses, where there are a lot of "people." They perform in the play, interject with humor, and are full of fun; in these places, you can see the distinction between "humans" and "animals."

However, the eyes of the audience seem to focus on the "animals," and only the strange performances of the "animals" are worthy of their praise. As for "people," if they are not women and do not have bare thighs, I am afraid they will not be as eye-catching as "animals"!

In fact, this is correct. They are watching "circus," and they are eager to see all kinds of wild animals that are not easy to see, so their attention to "people" is distracted. As for "women" and "thighs," that is an unexpected "bonus" for the average audience, getting some free fun. Chinese people seem to have an itch in their hearts when they talk about "getting some free fun," not to mention the young people, even the old people are not necessarily reliable!

In Shanghai, there is no opportunity to see monkey shows with "national essence," while the Haikingbo Circus Country has risen to take its place.

The former can fool the villagers more than enough, but the latter has caused the people of Shanghai to go wild for it!

I have not investigated what the word of mouth is for those who have seen the Haikingbo Circus. However, the declaration issued by Haikingbo in Shanghai cannot help but make me worry about China's "international status"!

According to him, he wants to collect all kinds of rare birds and exotic animals in China, and also wants to invite Chinese people to join their circus and show their faces in various countries.

This...um...what "people" do we have in China who can join the circus? If we ask "sellers of dog skin plaster" to make up the numbers, it would be really inappropriate. "Martial arts troupes" seem to lack "gentleman" demeanor, it is truly a sigh of lack of talent!

As for rare birds and exotic animals, it is really shameful to say that what can we offer to him in China? In the past, China did produce "Elaphurus davidianus" and other ferocious beasts, but they had long been subdued by Jiang Ziya in a loud shout of "evil animal"! In addition, the birds are not rare, and the beasts are not exotic, and there is nothing!

China is truly a "poor" country! But the audience in the circus last time was so crowded that it could be! This is enough to comfort Haikingbo of Anhui!

The Great Traffic Light 296

— Tong Chu

When the traffic light on the opposite side glared with its goldfish-like eyes, the rickshaw puller on this side held back the forward-moving carriage, the car driver turned the stop button, and the "puff puff puff" motorcycle just roared there; everything that was advancing on this side stopped. Everyone raised their eyes, hoping that the traffic light would change color immediately, glancing sideways at the vehicles passing arrogantly in front. The police officer on the traffic light platform blew his whistle, the color of the traffic light changed, and everyone hurriedly turned the machine parts, passing by more vigilantly than fleeing from a fire. At this time, on the road that could just pass, both sides of the intersection also bit the forward-moving vehicles, and they had no choice but to wait silently.

The bustling city is truly a bloody place! Tigers are leaping wildly, and jackals are chasing. Second after second, there is no escape from the terror of death. The great and bright traffic light, it jumps high, its eyes are wide open, its eyes are terrible! The wildly leaping tigers and jackals are subdued, and they pass by stealthily under its command.

We yearn for the great traffic light to jump into people's hearts; then "suspicion" and "hatred" will not occur. We yearn for the great traffic light to jump into this deformed society; then the weak will not be preyed upon.

Black Gold Seal and Black Gold Pestle 297

— Qing Fan

Black gold is a rare treasure in the world. During the Qing Dynasty, there were two items made of black gold: one was the black gold seal of Shi Dakai, the Wing King of the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom. Shi was in the army and hung it by his side, never leaving it for a moment, loving it no less than his own life. Later, when attacking Sichuan, he was defeated by the Qing army Tang Junmen, and his seal was also obtained by Tang. By the time of the Republic of China, the Sichuan War broke out repeatedly, and Tang's descendants could not protect it. It was seized by a powerful man, and recently it was rumored to have fallen into the hands of a soldier named Li. The central government had telegraphed Liu Xiang to inquire, but there was no whereabouts yet. Another black gold product is the medicine pestle of the He Tongren Pharmacy in Guangdong. The handle of the pestle is made of ebony, and the hammer of the pestle is decorated with black gold. Although the volume is not very large, it can be used to crush and grind hard medicinal materials easily. Moreover, the medicine ground by it is also quite effective. For example, the most famous black gold eye drops of the pharmacy are used to treat all eye diseases and external hemorrhoids and boils, and they are truly effective in ten thousand trials. This medicine was created more than a hundred years ago and sold in South China and overseas. It has considerable influence. Recently, the three major companies in Shanghai have also sold it, and it is highly trusted by society. It is said that the medicine pestle is still in the pharmacy, and it is treasured as a family heirloom. Non-relatives and descendants cannot easily touch it.

Royalty Payment Procedures 299

The royalty payment time of this museum is from the 6th to the 10th of each month, and then from the 16th to the 20th, excluding Sundays, from 2:00 pm to 4:00 pm every day, paid by the accounting office of this museum. Please prepare a slip with the same seal as the original manuscript and go directly to collect it. If you collect several months together, you must prepare a slip with a seal separately for each month so that it can be attached to the ledger. As for the seal section, regardless of the length of the article or the number of submissions each month, please stamp each article for verification of the seal when collecting royalties. If you do not stamp the seal, it will be regarded as unpaid. Furthermore, the royalty period starts from the date of publication and expires after six months. If there are still any uncollected at that time, it will be considered that you do not wish to receive the royalty, and the account will be canceled to end it. Northeast Four Company Commanders 300

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 19: Wanting to Leave, Yet Reluctant, They Recall Past Events in the Same Car; Half-Crying, Half-Laughing, Leaning on a Pillow in the Sickly Autumn

Madam Jiang immediately leaned her head into the curtain and asked Guizhi, "Girl, what's wrong with you?" Guizhi had her eyes half-open, and only when she suddenly heard her mother's call did she open them and look. At the same time, her face felt icy cold, and she knew it was tears flowing down her face, which her mother had seen. In her heart, she thought, if her mother knew this secret, how terrible would that be? So she frowned, slightly smiled, and said, "I feel unwell all over, uncomfortable in my heart, probably caught a chill." Madam Jiang stood in front of the bed-platform, stared at her face for a while, and then said, "You're really like a child. If you catch a chill, just lie down under the covers for a while, why are you crying?" Guizhi reached out and grabbed a corner of the quilt, rubbing her eyes, and said, "Who's crying? These are tears from a fever." Seeing her smile, although it looked somewhat forced, she couldn't quite consider it to be from sadness; perhaps she really couldn't bear the illness and shed tears. So she asked her, "Then lie down properly; do you want me to cook some porridge for you?" Guizhi frowned and said, "No! If I did that, then I'd really look like I'm sick. Just leave me alone, let me lie down." As she spoke, she turned over and went to sleep on the inside of the bed-platform. Madam Jiang saw that she seemed to be a little impatient with being sick, so she didn't bother her anymore. When Guizhi first lay down, she only felt tired, but now that she had been lying on the bed-platform for a long time, she felt as soft as cotton, and she didn't even want to turn over. She felt drowsy and lay like this until the afternoon, and her body indeed felt comfortable, and she forgot all her troubles. But this was only for a short time; around seven o'clock in the afternoon, she had already woken up. (261)

Small Recipes

A Discussion on Winter Tonics: Yam Puree - Food is Better Than Medicine - 301

— Ji Hongshan

Yam puree really has a delightful taste; it tastes good hot, and it tastes good cold. Upscale restaurants in Tianjin and Beiping sell it, and it's quite expensive, but not all of it is purely yam. Often, you pay a lot of money but don't get to eat the real thing. Here, I'll introduce how to make it, and yam is a famous tonic. Eating it now at the turn of autumn and winter is naturally much better than taking tonics. First, wash the whole yams clean, put them in a pot, and boil them with water for one or two hours until they are soft and mushy. Then peel off the outer skin, revealing the completely clean yam flesh. Put it in a stone mortar and mash it into a mud-like consistency, making sure there are no small pieces left. When eating it, put it in a pot and cook it with a small amount of cooked lard until it's thoroughly heated. Add white sugar to taste, and heat it thoroughly. In this way, the lard is also absorbed by the yam, and the taste is excellent.

Lard Stewed Dates

"Lard Stewed Dates" is not a bourgeois food. Usually, everyone knows about it, so there's no need to talk much about it. The method is to put good dates with a large amount of lard in a pot on top of the rice cooker and steam them for more than ten days. The dates will become plump and absorb a lot of oil. When people eat this, it increases the oil in the body and generates more heat. Fat people should definitely avoid eating it, otherwise, they will become unbearably ripe by next summer.

Walnuts and White Sugar

Pound the walnuts into small pieces, mix in an appropriate amount of white sugar and lard. It really invigorates the blood and strengthens the brain. People who drink alcohol can use it as a snack, which is very suitable. Even just mixing a cup of it with hot water every morning and eating it is very beneficial. However, when peeling the walnuts, you must peel off the inner skin, which is a bit more troublesome.

Nantang Water Chestnuts

This year's water chestnuts are two or three times cheaper than in previous years. Those who are financially well-off can eat more of them and replace breakfast, which is not impossible. This year, you can buy more than two pounds for one yuan, while last year, you had to buy one pound for more than two yuan, which is a big difference. It is enough to indicate that the rural economy has reached an extreme state of bankruptcy.

Milk

Ordinary milk, some of which are made into types A and B, has been tested by the Shanghai Municipal Council Health Department and divided into types A and B. Type A has three times fewer organisms than type B, and has already undergone disinfection procedures, so it's okay to drink it cold. But type B is not. When boiling type A milk, you only need to warm it slightly. If you boil it, the vitamins in the milk will also be burned off at the same time. Therefore, it is more appropriate to pay for the more expensive type A milk. Many milk farms opened by Chinese people themselves also have type A, which is worth recommending. Every half-pint costs about six yuan or less per month.

Eggs

A large number of eggs are produced in rural areas every year, and many are consumed in winter. Its efficacy and price need no further explanation from the author. It is also very relevant to the relief of rural areas. And for people with jobs, eating them in the morning is much more convenient than anything else. Especially in the inland areas, you can buy fifty or sixty very fresh eggs for one yuan, and the nutrients are enough to抵過抵過 ginseng and bird's nest, etc.

Beef Juice

Just put the chopped beef in a pot specifically for steaming beef juice, without adding anything else, and simmer it over a low fire overnight. The beef will all turn into beef juice. Chicken essence is made in the same way, but the internal organs, head, and feet are not used. The remaining dried meat can be dried and made into braised beef or coffee beef. Just cook it slightly and it will be soft and transparent, which can be used as a side dish. Two dimes worth of raw beef can be cooked twice, enough for one person for one meal.

Soy Milk

Everyone knows that soybeans are rich in protein and vitamins. Therefore, soy milk made from soybeans (commonly known as tofu pudding) is also very popular among hardworking comrades. A big cup in the morning doesn't cost more than five copper coins, which is really very affordable. There are stores that specialize in selling soy milk in the market. The author has not tried it, so I apologize for not introducing it. Making it yourself is naturally the most reliable and clean. The day before, soak the raw soybeans in water until they are plump, then mash them with a stone mortar and add water to filter them. Mash and filter them again, about three or four times, until only渣滓 only渣滓 remains. When eating, boil it over the fire and add a little white sugar. This is the cheapest and cleanest.

Most of the popular winter tonics are here. Other gelatinous medicines, ginseng, bird's nest, and white fungus are not affordable for everyone, and they are not necessarily suitable for everyone's constitution. The author will stop writing here.

Professor's Secrets 302

— Mingchun

A certain professor described the secrets of being a professor. I record it to provide to those who aspire to be professors.

1. When going to the lecture hall, you should often mention your experience of studying abroad, such as "When I was in New York before." As for the names of your teachers, such as "John," "Smith," etc., you may as well mention them more often. It would be even better if you could say that you had a certain friendship with them.

2. When taking on a certain subject, you must first collect reference books from various countries about this subject, and often say that you will add some criticism! Pretend to have read it! Finally, you must declare that there is not a single Chinese reference book that is worth reading.

3. Take leave often to avoid people saying that you are not old enough, and at the same time, you can give the students some relaxation.

4. When criticizing other people's theories, it is best not to be twelve-point worship, and you should often use the phrase "But my opinion is." In your own lecture notes, use the word "鄙意" (my humble opinion) more often to avoid being accused of plagiarism.

5. During the exam, you should sit quietly and read the newspaper, and occasionally look out the window.

6. As for state affairs, speak less to students about them (in fact, no matter how deep the national crisis is, we have few reactions in our hearts). Before hearing the sound of imperialist cannons, you may as well advocate the theory of saving the country through reading, which is what a scholar should be like.

The above points are for temporarily keeping your job. As for those who want to use teaching as a stepping stone to climb to the road of bureaucracy, I'm sorry, but it doesn't apply.

Flour and Imported Wheat Prices Set, Flour Weakens 318

After the opening of the flour market this morning, prices for all months showed a trend of rising first and then falling. With quotations for imported wheat rising in Chicago by nine "jiao" (a unit of currency) and in Canada by two "jiao," market sentiment remained firm at the opening, continuing a one "fen" (a unit of currency) improvement from the previous day's closing. However, the market soon turned soft. The selling of imported wheat was very active, with government-loaned wheat and Argentine wheat quoted at very low prices, only four yuan without tax and only four yuan and five or six "jiao" with tax. At the current market price, selling already yields a profit, so market sentiment became very weak. At the afternoon opening, it was heard that domestic factories had transacted a shipment of Argentine imported wheat at four yuan and four and a half "fen," leading to large-scale selling of over 200,000 units. Some factories also sold slightly, causing the market to fall across the board. With overseas spot wheat quoted so cheaply, future prospects are likely to be variable. As a result, the current month fell three "fen" compared to the previous day, January fell three "fen" and seven and a half "li" (a smaller unit of currency), February fell four and a half "fen," March and April fell three "fen" and seven and a half "li," and May fell four "fen" and seven and a half "li."

The wheat market opened this morning with a mixed but ultimately falling trend. Although imported wheat quotations rose by nine "jiao" in Chicago and two "jiao" in Canada, the market lacked vitality. Transactions were sluggish due to the fact that, despite occasional fluctuations in the price of standard imported wheat, the spot market was ultimately burdened by oversupply, making dumping inevitable. For this reason, buyers were apprehensive. At the afternoon opening, with the flour market having turned from rising to falling, the sentiment for all months also softened. It was heard that some parties were also engaging in hedging sales, leading to further instability in the market. As a result, the current month fell four "fen" compared to the previous day, January fell four "fen," February fell five "fen," and March fell five "fen." Spot wheat market transactions were very few. Top-quality goods opened at three "jiao" one, Shandong wheat opened at four yuan three "jiao," and Yaowan wheat at four yuan two "jiao" seven "fen," totaling three hundred packages, reportedly handled by Huafeng.

Tram Stop 327

— Meng Ke

At the intersection of a bustling thoroughfare, on the corner of the sidewalk to the left, stood a telephone pole, washed grey-white by the rain. Nailed to it was a red-lacquered iron sign, neatly inscribed in white paint with the name of the Fairweather Road and the fare schedule. Beneath the iron sign, there were piles of advertisements for "Milky White Cure-Alls," their characters already somewhat blurred. Beside the pole, as usual, stood a crowd of impatient people, clamoring, sometimes craning their necks, peering anxiously at the end of the road: their faces generally tense and resentful. But slowly pacing back and forth, as if eternally attached to this telephone pole, was a stooped, wizened, monkey-like female beggar. Though it was deep autumn, she wore only a piece of burlap, caked with mud, wrapped around her body. Her face was the color of vegetables. Her yellow hair, soaked by the rain and then dried into brittle strands, always hung down her arms. But anyone who caught sight of the raw, festering hole in the center of her face, dripping with yellow pus, would feel as if something was missing, and immediately think of the horrors of syphilis.

She moved slowly through the crowd, her coffee-colored, dry-twig-like hand stretching out from under the burlap, opening, bowing and smiling, politely addressing all sorts of people. The impatient people grew even more impatient, ladies tightened their grip on their purses, frowned, swung their large hips, and hurried away. She seemed quite sensible, didn't pester them. Those who she followed closely were the short-clad men in "hunting caps," reeking of gasoline. She still addressed them as "masters," but the men weren't necessarily pleased by this. At first, they too shook their heads, looking embarrassed, but eventually, out of the pockets holding measuring tapes or iron pliers, they'd fish out a couple of copper coins, though some, after extending their rough hands, would reluctantly pull them back.

In this rather busy occupation, she lived.

Until dusk, when the colorful electric lights of the grand stores lit up, she seemed to notice her own fatigue and hunger, but she didn't leave the area. Leaning against the telephone pole, the raw, festering hole in the center of her face still dripped with yellow pus, as if she was dozing off, or as if she was longing for the clatter of bowls and chopsticks and the sounds of song and laughter from the restaurant across the street.

Business at the restaurant was especially good at night. At the front door, cars and chartered carriages formed a serpentine line. Jovial gentlemen with big bellies hopped out of the cars, some followed by formidable toughs. The carriages, however, were occupied by pretty young ladies, who giggled and chatted, with an old woman hobbling along behind them, straight into the front door.

Beside the telephone pole, a crowd of impatient people still stood, clamoring, until there was no more sound of bowls and chopsticks or song and laughter from the restaurant.

Impressions of Watching a Circus Performance in Guanhai Jingbo 328

— Ye Yongye

Two, The Horse's Dance

Only one horse came out, desolately.

But although there was only one horse, this horse was very tall, its coat pure black. Astride the horse was a woman dressed entirely in white. In the light, the colors were extremely harmonious.

Seeing this horse walking slowly in the arena, I was almost perplexed.

Suddenly, someone tossed out a "modern" word from behind: "Dance."

Fortunately, I was "blessed" to have studied for a few years, and understood the meaning of "Dance." Examining the horse's footsteps and listening to the music from the platform, the horse was indeed "Dancing."

I felt a bit of interest and began to watch attentively, thinking that I had never been to a dance hall. Although I had never seen people "Dance," being able to see a horse "Dance" was not a bad stroke of luck. The horse's "Dance" was indeed quite good: as the music began on the platform, it began to sway back and forth and dance. When the sound slowed down, its steps slowed down; when it sped up, its steps sped up. When it became urgent, it lifted its front hooves and kicked left and right in the air. When it stopped, it stopped immediately and stood still.

But of course, controlling it was the woman riding on its back.

Everyone in the arena clapped.

I clapped too.

There was nothing to criticize, given the way its steps matched the rhythm of the music. No one could help but admire it, given its intelligence and ability to learn such a technique.

And so, the horse danced with increasing delight, even wagging its tail, as if it was keeping time.

I felt a pang of shame.

And yet, for the sake of this horse, I also felt a pang of shame. I felt that since this horse was so tall and so intelligent, why wasn't it galloping on the battlefield or in the countryside? Instead, it let a woman ride on its back and manipulate it, telling it to do this and that, to do so and so?

Was being a puppet of a woman more glorious than relying on its own strength to survive?

I didn't believe so.

But things in the world are truly hard to say. We don't need to speak ill of the horse. As for humans, aren't there many promising young people, like this horse, who want to be a woman's puppet, letting her ride on their backs and do whatever she pleases? As long as the reins in her hand move, how happily does the ridden person jump!

You don't think about how ugly this looks in the eyes of others, and seem to believe that the woman riding on your back is truly your master. Putting all your fantasies and hopes into your own steps, you let the mocking people clap and laugh beside you in your illusions, and you yourself, like this horse, sway and strut along step by step.

You will believe that this is your happiness.

"Happiness, happiness!" you shout wildly.

And so, you dance even more vigorously, perhaps wagging your tail to estimate how much happiness you have, just like the horse wagging its tail to keep time.

I know that I once "Danced" like this horse, and my face couldn't help but turn red.

Today, I see the ugliness of my past posture.

I must thank this horse.

Small Notes from a Traveler's Window 329

— Shu Liu

Zhu Shuzhen is known for her poetry, but her prose is also exceedingly elegant, and her calligraphy is not weak either. She has a small-script copy of Su Ruolan's "Brocade-Weaving Revolving Sphere Poem," to which she attached her own small note. In addition to introducing the history of Su Hui and interpreting the "Revolving Sphere Poem," this note contains many sentiments. The final section reads:

"I have meticulously copied and interpreted it, keeping it in my satchel for eleven years. Since I married, I have been burdened by worldly affairs, my head aches and I fear the wind, my thin wrist trembles, and I cannot control myself. Could it be that I am driven by curiosity? Alas! With Ruolan's skill, she could weave it in the past; but without my labor, it could not be understood in the present. Why are the ages different but the ambitions so similar? I wonder who in the future will study this diagram. I hope that those who see it will not think that a woman should not engage in internal cultivation but be boastful of engaging in literature and art, which is not beautiful. If so, they are not talent-loving scholars. Please do not dare to argue, and may those who share my heart be like me. Alas, I sell it." The note ends with nineteen characters: "Written by recluse Zhu Shuzhen in the auspicious month of April in the third year of Shaoding in the Huang Song Dynasty." From this, we can glimpse a facet of Shuzhen's life and her inner indignation regarding the understanding of women in feudal society; as for the article, that is a secondary matter.

Seven

Yuan Zhonglang greatly praised the book "Jin Ping Mei," as recorded in his "Weishui Xuan Diary":

"November 5th (Wanli 43rd year). Shen Boyuan brought the novel 'Jin Ping Mei' collected by his uncle Jingqian. It is mostly extremely obscene vulgar talk, and the flames are far inferior to 'Water Margin.' Yuan Zhonglang praised it profusely, which is also excessive curiosity."

Although Li Rihua and Yuan Hongdao belonged to the same school in terms of ideological system, they did not agree on many points. The difference in their understanding of the book "Jin Ping Mei" suggests this. Yuan has a poem "Ode to Junshi," which was written for Li and included in the book "Crazy Words."

Eight

From my notebooks of several years ago, I came across a short poem that I copied at the time—"Leopard Order." The poem reads:

"Rare goods are worth hoarding, as the saying goes.

As the saying goes, I'm waiting to sell thousands of miles of territory to the Yuan Dynasty.

Unlike Jing Ke, I don't use useless tricks to acquire Dukang.

Master, you're like Zhang Song presenting Yizhou in your own hands,

True goods need a high price."

The source was not specified at the time. I don't know if it is from the zaju "Zhang Song Presents the Map" in "Selections of Yuan Operas." Today, when I discuss it again, I feel something else. Such satire can be described as extremely clever.

Nine

There are many poems describing the hardship of life. Lu You's "Young, traveling far without a hundred miles, one hunger forces me to walk to the ends of the earth," and Zhong Que's "Overworked and old, it's difficult to support eight mouths," "Fearing the cold but insisting on coming into the cold, our generation is not as good at making a living as geese." Such poems, at least until today, are "ever new."

Ten

Yellow leaves are most evocative in poetry. After writing the article "Talking about Yellow Leaves," I saw many more. For example, Wu Shaoyun's "White lotus withers, people seek the shrine, yellow leaves bleak, magpies call in the village," "Autumn sounds gather in the yellow gathering, mountain shadows in the evening smoke," and "Bamboo light like a sea, green clouds stop, distant temple bells heard several times. Walking to the end of Zhaodi, yellow leaves slightly, across the river the mountain color reaches the door" (from Lingyin to Taoguang) can be said to be rare good lines. Yuan Zhonglang's poems also sometimes use "yellow leaves," but there are not many good lines. However, from his "Splitting yellow leaves to stop children from crying," we can know that "yellow leaves" still have other uses. I remember that Wu Linzheng of the Ming Dynasty wrote to his uncle Shengbai, "Also, I heard that the uncle did not enter the capital gate with a single piece of paper, which is difficult to bear in old age. Now, the essential passes are tired of fruit and meat, and the small yellow leaves are not enough to stop children from crying. What about saving them to keep peace and integrity? The uncle means to say this?" His meaning is the same as Yuan's poem, using "yellow leaves" as a metaphor for something that cannot satisfy people. I specially attach this note to supplement the shortcomings of the previous article.

The Two Brothers (51) 330

— Written by Maupassant, Translated by Li Weike

But no, she had deceived him, she had stolen his tenderness, stolen his sincerity, and she ought to have been without fault to be worthy of him, as all mothers should be for their sons. Because he felt that she had committed a greater crime against him than against his father, that surge of anger that arose in him almost turned to hatred.

The love of men and women is originally a contract of desire. When love wanes, the sin is merely infidelity; but when that woman becomes a mother, then because nature has entrusted her with a race, her obligations are greater. If she cannot insist at this time, she is cowardly, base, and shameless.

"In short, it's not a bad thing to have a modest fortune and live a comfortable life," Father Roland suddenly said, stretching his legs out under the table, sipping his glass of Cassis (liquor made from black raspberries) as he did every night. "I hope Zhan will often invite us to eat elaborate dinners in the future. Even if I sometimes get a little sick because of it, I won't care."

Then he turned to his woman and said:

"Since you've finished eating, go find that portrait. I'd be happy to see him again."

She stood up, took a candle, and went out. Afterwards, the deliberation was actually only three minutes, but to Pierre it seemed like a long time. Mother Roland smiled as she came in with the portrait framed with old-fashioned gold borders. She was holding the ring on the frame when she said, "I almost found it right away."

The doctor reached out his hand first. He took the portrait, stretched out his arm, and examined it from a little distance. Then, feeling his mother watching him, he slowly raised his eyes and looked at his younger brother for comparison. Given his agitated mood at that time, he almost wanted to say, "Wow, it's just like Zhan." Although he didn't say those terrible words, he used this method of comparing the living face with the face in the painting to express his thoughts.

True, the two faces had some identical organizations; they had the same beard and the same forehead, but there was nothing obvious enough to make people declare: "Wow, this is the father, this is the son." It's better to say that it's a kind of family appearance, a similarity in appearance that is manifested by the same blood. But to Pierre, what was more certain than the appearance of these two faces was that his mother stood up, turned her back, and slowly pretended to be putting sugar and Cassis away in a cabinet.

She already knew that he knew, or at least that he suspected!

"Let me see," Roland said.

Pierre handed him the portrait, he moved the candle closer to look at it carefully; then he whispered in a moved voice:

"Poor child! We knew him when he looked like this. Alas, how quickly time passes! He was indeed a"

"Handsome man at that time, and his actions were so interesting, wasn't he, Louise?"

Seeing that his woman didn't answer him, he continued:

"And what a good nature he had! I never saw him angry. Well, it's over now, nothing is left"

"Besides the property left to Zhan. In short, we can swear that this person showed himself to be a faithful good friend until his death. He didn't even forget us when he was dying."

Now it was Zhan's turn to reach out and take the portrait. He stared at it for a while, then said with regret: "As for me, I don't recognize him at all. I only remember his white hair falling about his face."

Then he handed the portrait back to his mother, who glanced at the portrait quickly, and then quickly turned her eyes away, as if she were a little frightened; but then she said in her natural tone:
