My Distorted Environment 331

— Fiery Flame

Speaking from a certain standpoint, it was obviously an immoral act. Although, on the scale of immorality, it had been acknowledged since ancient times and didn't count as a crime, upright gentlemen couldn't help but feel some disgust. As for me, from then until now, I've been certain: the environment forced me to become so distorted.

The matter occurred in the nineteenth year [of the Republic, i.e., 1930], at which time the Shanghai publishing world was in the heyday of introducing and compiling new social science books. The market was much more prosperous than it is now. What was posted on the signboards of bookstores wasn't "big sale" or the tiresome "half-price bargain sale," but rather "welcome to browse," "new book release," or "publication preview." The news disclosed in newspapers daily was also mostly publishing news. Because of this, the bookstore owners all had a bit of pride, their bellies protruding as they sat on the counter behind the brass railing, looking as if they were rising higher and higher in status. Book prices became more expensive day by day. A small booklet of only a hundred-odd pages often sold for more than seven or eight jiao [cents]; if it was a famous work and also thicker, then you couldn't even think of getting your hands on it for less than two yuan. Another thing was that books published not long ago would suddenly "increase in price according to the original price plus one," in short, they were incredibly expensive.

This means it was the era of the bookstore owners. They had grasped the minds of the intellectual class under the wheels of the times. Since the books published were speculative and to their liking, the prices naturally became "even higher than before."

However, there were indeed many poor young men who deeply couldn't bear this kind of grandstanding, and could only quench their thirst by looking at plums, dazed by advertisements. But poor young men mostly liked to read a bit, especially in that kind of emerging publishing atmosphere, eagerly crying out for knowledge. At that time, I was loafing around in a national school. Although the school was national, the library was pitifully poor. Precisely because the new books in the bookstores at that time were said to have some reactionary color, unlike the Three Principles of the People, which spoke of reason in a proper and orderly manner, the library director didn't pay attention to these when drawing up the book list, and only cared about purchasing ancient books in large quantities. I myself was too poor to stand up straight, but my desire for knowledge was very strong. Under these circumstances, I had repeatedly thought about "stealing books."

However, at that time, my mind was still somewhat constrained. I felt that I was a dignified university student, and "stealing" was truly not appropriate for me to commit lightly. If something went wrong, how could I face anyone? Even if I wasn't thrown into prison, I still wouldn't be able to account for myself, so I just thought and hesitated, not daring to try it lightly.

One day, attracted by an advertisement—"welcome to browse"—I went to the so-called Culture Street. It was truly lively. Every bookstore was crowded to the point where water couldn't leak through. Buying, reading, flipping through, perhaps there were many comrades of mine inside. So, in the midst of the crowd, I attempted the opening act of "stealing." My heart was uneasy, as if there was a buzzing sound in my ears, and the face of the oily boss was shaking before my eyes. However, I ultimately triumphed. On the tram ride back to school, I flipped through the pages, one by one. I smiled, desperately suppressing the "counterattack" mentality. Then, I performed many more acts, many days. So, my bed, desk, and shelves were filled with the new books I had longed for all my life. I smiled at any time. I cherished and caressed them, read them. Originally, I didn't have many books at all, but later I suddenly became a book-collecting nouveau riche. To be frank, they were all stolen.

However, in the past few years, they have gradually decreased again. Now, there are almost none left. Either they were lent to friends and never returned, or they seemed to have run away one by one, just like they were visiting each house. But I am already satisfied with them, because they have already made a contribution to me, enabling me to barely manage to pick up a pen.

The Four-Six Split 332

— Sword Screen

Our neighbor, Mrs. Tang, because she lost a beloved daughter last year, made a special trip to Jiangwan yesterday to call upon an old woman who communicates with the dead. It is said to be very effective. Not only can she answer the father's name and occupation, but she even knows that she went to see a movie yesterday. Do you think it's strange or not?

My family's younger brother, Zhi-di, sacrificed himself in the Shanghai battle two years ago. Thinking of his heroic spirit, his soul should also be more effective than someone who died of illness. So, I really want to contact him and comfort my pain of losing a wing. But it is said that the rules for contacting the dead require sending a servant to register overnight, so that the souls can be found calmly and not mistaken for someone else. This makes it difficult for me, a poor scholar who has never had a servant. However, after all, brotherhood is deep, so after hesitating for a while, I decided to temporarily lose my identity as a teacher and go to register myself.

As I stepped into the gate of this old woman who communicates with the dead, I suddenly heard a very familiar voice coming from the long window inlaid with oyster shells. I stopped to ponder for a while, and then remembered that it was A-gen, the cook from the Tang family.

"Why are you only giving me one yuan and twenty cents?" A-gen asked.

"Yes, we usually split the commission with the message carriers four-six. Your wife took out three yuan and sixty cents. After deducting the sixty cents for incense and candles, isn't that three-fourths, one yuan and twenty cents, for you? Moreover, when you came to register, the information you provided was not very detailed. You didn't mention the young mistress's name, which almost made me mess up on the spot. If I weren't a thirty-year veteran, able to roll my tongue and get through it, things would have gone bad," replied an old woman's voice.

After hearing this fragment of their conversation, it was as if a ladle of cold water had been poured over my head, abruptly dropping my enthusiasm to a freezing point. So, I quickly backed up and fled from this ghostly door.

The Dream of Higher Examinations 333

— Hui Gu

"What a rare opportunity, the higher examinations are being held again this year. Well, I'm going to try it out."

"Originally, when people go to take higher examinations, they wouldn't announce it to others, because once they fail, they feel very embarrassed. Only I am not like that, I insist on announcing it to everyone, but I also ask everyone to forgive me. Once I fail, please don't laugh at me."

"Nonsense, nonsense, would we laugh at you? Besides, Mr. Zhu is also very easygoing," the classmates said, with a very polite tone and a look of hoping that Mr. Zhu would continue speaking.

"As for why I want to take the higher examinations, the reasons are very complicated. I was most excited by that sentence of Merton's, he said: 'The weak give up opportunities, only the weak can seize opportunities,' hey, how exciting is that! I think this sentence is really valuable, so I desperately seize this opportunity. Another layer is that the fortune teller said that I have a prosperous official career, and there will be success within this year. In any case, although this can't be considered a meaningful attraction, it is also very touching to me. Besides, being a teacher seems very noble in name, but in reality, this chalk life of a teacher is the most unfortunate, because this profession doesn't seem to suit my personality. For this reason, I want to change the environment again, so I go to take the exam... there are many reasons, please forgive me for not saying more!" Mr. Zhu suddenly stopped at this point, he looked at the ceiling with a smile, perhaps he was thinking about something.

The classmates sat happily, and Mr. Zhu continued:

"This time, I am taking the general administration aspect of the exam. If I pass, I will also be able to be a county magistrate. The sentence is that it is very difficult to be admitted at all. The first exam requires taking the second exam. The first exam includes finance, economics, the Three Principles of the People, Chinese, history, geography, etc. The second exam is even more annoying. As far as the first exam is concerned, I already feel a lot of difficulty, and now that I am going to take the exam, I have to temporarily hug the Buddha's feet and open the night train, alas, just like when you are going to take the exam."

"Hush, hush, alas,"

"Regardless of anything else, even if I only attend the higher examinations, I will gain some life experience, which may help my writing. I will go to Nanjing next week, so I will ask Mr. Ma to take my place temporarily,"

"Oh, County Magistrate Zhu, County Magistrate..." the classmates laughed mischievously.

Two weeks have passed, the higher examinations have also been taken, and our Chinese teacher - Mr. Zhu - has also returned!

"County Magistrate, County Magistrate is here!" the classmates laughed secretly when Mr. Zhu came into the classroom.

Mr. Zhu also looked at us with a smile.

"Mr. Zhu, what is the result of the exam?"

"It's just so-so, I think I'm doing well, right? Why? Because I see that many people have handed in blank papers, which is ten thousand times worse than me - and I want to tell you that some of the difficult questions, I circled around and wrote a big sheet, but in fact they were all irrelevant words, just perfunctory, but maybe I can get a few points from them, you have to know that this is really a way to take the exam! Some kinds of exams are good, some kinds of exams are not good, probably, on average, there will always be a passing score!" Mr. Zhu recited with great interest.

"Then isn't a county magistrate stable?" Old Wang asked interestingly.

"No, I can't decide!"

"Don't be polite."

"The results will be announced in five days, and then I will know!" Mr. Zhu said so definitely.

"Mr. Zhu will definitely pass the exam in five days! Definitely, it must be a county magistrate"

"Is Mr. Zhu fierce as a county magistrate?"

"Chuckle" He smiled!

"Ha! Ha! County Magistrate!"

The announcement has been published, but we didn't see Mr. Zhu's name. Ha, ha, not only Mr. Zhu alone, but also we, everyone had a "dream of higher examinations"!

One Night of Terror 334

— Hui Liu

As long as they are from Wangjiaji [Wang Family Village], everyone knows that Wang the Rich is very wealthy; at the same time, his fields are also the most in this area. There are more than 400 households in the entire village, more than half of whom make a living by farming. The fields they cultivate are all owned by Wang the Rich. Therefore, he has some influence in the village. His home is in a tall, black-lacquered gate that is ten feet high at the north end of the village. The neighbors are all piles of broken houses—the dwellings of the poor. Among these many dilapidated houses, Wang the Rich's residence is even more spacious and magnificent!

At this time, it was the middle of winter. Because it hadn't rained for a long time, a thick layer of sand and dust had accumulated on the ground. It was blown by the merciless north wind, making it feel particularly cold and annoying. As evening approached, the wind grew stronger, and the night god gradually swallowed everything in space. On the road from the village to the north end, in addition to the footsteps of one or two pedestrians, only the sound of the whistling wind could be heard. By nine or ten o'clock at night, even the pedestrians had disappeared. In the distance, a few barks of dogs were heard. Immediately, three dark shadows窜出 [cuan chu - darted out] from a broken house a hundred or so steps from Wang's house. From the faint starlight, you could see that they were tall and sturdy. It seemed that each person was also holding a dark instrument in their hand. A burst of chaotic footsteps stopped in front of a tall gate at the north end. Needless to say, it was Wang the Rich's residence.

That night, Wang the Rich had just returned from the countryside and was lying on the bed smoking and relaxing. He was showing off a roll of banknotes to his wife, who was standing beside him with great interest.

"Look - these brand-new banknotes. Wang Shun and his nephew Wang Da were in a family lawsuit. Today, I actually persuaded them to reconcile willingly, and they each gave me twenty yuan"! Wang the Rich spread out the banknotes one by one with great satisfaction. At the same time, he counted them one by one and said to his wife.

"Of course, without money! Who would be happy to do these irrelevant things? Didn't I ask you to buy a necklace the day before yesterday? You said you would buy it when this money came in. I'm going to wear it out the day after tomorrow"! Wang the Rich's wife made this request to her husband with a half-happy, half-annoyed expression.

"I know! I'll go tomorrow"! Wang the Rich replied solemnly.

As he said this, he finished smoking one cigarette, took a sip of tea, and slowly exhaled a puff of black smoke from his mouth. He was just about to put the second cigarette in his mouth when he suddenly heard a sound. A feeling arose in his dizzy brain: "Is someone coming to talk to me at this time? Yes, that must be it." Film Special Issue

Famous Failures in Film History (Part 1) 339

— Translated by Jia Gu

A person with even a slight degree of film observation can usually recognize a successful film. But can we similarly recognize a failed film? Of course, I'm not referring to mediocre productions or clumsy craftsmanship, but to first-class blockbusters whose failure impacts the rise and fall of the entire studio and the success or failure of a major star's career.

A blockbuster is like a bet before its public release. The bigger the bet, the more severe the failure. But what is it that orchestrates success or failure in the shadows? You probably often hear about the production process of a successful film, from the search for a good story to the profit-making. You know who the victorious generals are, how they triumphed, and in what way. However, the history of film failures is no less rich than that of successes. But you rarely hear about who caused those failures, much less how or why they happened.

A major success on the screen invariably creates a major star or a major director, or both. But on the other hand, every failure ruins a person's reputation, shatters a person's future; or, if their reputation is deeply rooted and can withstand the storm, it will inevitably suffer a severe blow, including economic loss and damage to their honor.

The failures on the screen are like figures on a revolving lantern, countless and constantly changing. The comparison of their numbers seems ordained by fate, roughly equal. And the first failure often follows closely on the heels of the first major success. The great director D.W. Griffith made two big films. The one that will be remembered in history forever is *The Birth of a Nation*. But he also made *Intolerance*. The production of that second film cost $350,000, which was not only a huge sum at the time, but is still quite considerable even now. The making of that film was a major artistic gamble for Griffith, because he wanted to combine three different eras of world history into one historical film. As a result, although the film's content was rich and its program varied, it was a thankless task. Audiences were unwilling to jump from Babylon to France in the era of the Huguenots, and then jump again to modern America. It was like throwing a baseball and trying to hit three corners at the same time, but ending up not hitting any of them.

Speaking of the history of failures in the film industry, the strangest thing is that failures are often created by people who shouldn't fail. Their knowledge and experience should have been able to warn them of the path of ruin and prevent them from falling. Of course, the devil is always one step ahead. It takes great talent, great experience, and great capital to qualify for a great failure. Amateur artists and fledgling actors are not likely to go too far astray even if they take the wrong path. So, what is the root of great failure? In a nutshell, it can be said that individual vanity, exaggerated ambition, and the abuse of money are the elements that cause great failure. (To be continued)

Film Reviews

Review of "Christopher Strong" 340

— Moore

Of course, romances between men and women are the easiest to happen in society and are also the most "dramatic." Therefore, it is not without reason that events of men and women occupy the majority in movies. *Christopher Strong* is also a film with love between men and women as its theme.

Society is very complex and contradictory. Therefore, even in terms of men and women events, there are all kinds of attitudes presented to us. For an artist, dealing with a material is essentially their own understanding and opinion of a certain event. Therefore, even if a film uses the same love story as a theme, what we see is different.

*Christopher Strong* is a story of "two generations of love." The so-called two generations of love here does not show several different ways of love like "three generations of love." It only says that father and daughter both fall into the trap of love and cannot extricate themselves. We don't need to criticize the story itself. Let's see what the author's view on this story is?

"Shixia is already pregnant, deeply regrets her mistakes, and does not want Clay's reputation and happiness to be destroyed with her, so she resolutely soars into the sky and commits suicide by plane."

This is the end of the film, and it is also the author's opinion. The so-called Shixia here is a woman who is in love with a middle-aged man who is married, but they keep it secret, and finally, when it can no longer be hidden, she commits suicide for the sake of her lover's reputation. Behind this, we can see that the producers of *Christopher Strong* believe that it is disgraceful for a married man to be in love with a third party. This point is also confirmed by the fact that young Harry divorced and married young Monica, and this kind of thinking surrounded by traditional concepts is originally shared by a group of old artists. However, in *Christopher Strong*, the author publicly solves it as a problem.

When reading the novels of British writers, I am always amazed by their profound observations. They introduce an ordinary story to the readers in a "microscopic" way, and their method is similar to the anatomy of biologists, objectively to the point of being almost cruel. (Of course, they also have subjective opinions.) Now, the producers of *Christopher Strong* should first observe the truth of this story, think about the meaning of this story, and then emphasize a certain part, simplify a certain part, and express it more truthfully. However, the producers of *Christopher Strong* simply unfold the story in a mediocre way, and the old content makes it impossible to have a new form. What's more, this kind of story should pay attention to psychological analysis, such as the hesitation of a married man when he starts to fall in love with Shixia, and the complex psychology of his wife Jie Lan in preventing her daughter from falling in love with Harry. This conflict between emotion and reason is really the most worthwhile thing to grab in film, but the director of *Christopher Strong* completely abandons it.

The most regrettable thing is that the heroine of this film is originally very good at acting, but under the restrictions of the plot and the director, she has to reduce a lot of achievements.

Review of "I'm No Angel" - Paramount Production, Cathay Premiere - 341

— Ling He

I remember seeing *She Done Him Wrong* at the Guanglu Theater on May 20th this year, and Mae West's name began to leave a deep impression in my mind. Her special style added formal beauty to American films. According to the introduction of American film magazines, she is the most popular person among movie fans after Greta Garbo. Her box office numbers in the United States are even above Garbo, but in terms of money, it is far less than the Swedish Garbo, because the market is sluggish now and seat prices have been reduced.

But what is Mae West's magic? This is of course because she has a talent for acting, but because her dramatic art in this style can have a strong connection with American movie fans, which proves what they need. In a beautiful life, gentlemen are very much hoping to get enchanting temptation from women.

Indeed, she is a talented actress with unique achievements. It is said that her plays are all written by herself, so we have to admit that she is a superior talent.

Speaking of this work, I think the director is the first one who deserves praise. The most successful kind of happy mood fills the entire screen. From beginning to end, it is consistently bright and compact. Under the flexible wrist of director Wesley Ruggles, no small section is not delightful. For example, the court scene is generally difficult to control, because there are too many lines, which can easily make people feel dull, but here, the court scene is still so lively. Of course, most of the achievements should be attributed to Mae West.

Speaking of this, we must touch on the essence of the story. The heroine here is naturally a typical figure in the modern society of the golden country. In order to enjoy herself to the fullest, she does not hesitate to sell her body. She uses her entire body to exchange for a large amount of money from gentlemen. How many gentlemen get from her what they lack and cannot lack at the highest price. Of course, the playwright has great sympathy for the heroine. Although she recklessly falls, she is moved by the so-called true love and unites with the person she loves. Fortunately, the man she loves is not a poor and down-and-out poet, so it still consistently explains that this kind of woman cannot escape the life of jewelry. However, we cannot praise this kind of character, although she is the most reasonable product of society.

At the same time, the playwright uses the heroine's tone to scold the world. She laughs and scolds gentlemen, lawyers, and even dignified judges, who bow to her under her enchantment. I think such joking and scolding is really to the extreme. Just from this point alone, this story is already very commendable.

Several supporting roles are very good, but that Cary Grant makes people feel uncomfortable, at least he is not as pleasing as in *Eagle and the Hawk*.

Editor's note: Regarding this film, this magazine has specially invited Cheng Bugao, Li Fu, and Shen Xiling to conduct detailed research on the screenwriting and directing aspects in order to realize "constructive criticism." A long article will be published soon. Please pay attention to it!

Ye Qiuxin Commits Suicide - In "The Fire of Youth" - 342

— A Person of Passion

It is said that after Ye Qiuxin disrupted her lover Yu Guang's wedding, she returned and sulked alone in the house. Yu Guang rushed in angrily, and the first sentence was: "Hello, you have ruined everything for me, I want your life!" Ye Qiuxin saw that the situation was not right, so she took out a pistol from the drawer and said to Yu Guang: "Can you forgive me? It's all my fault. But, Yu Guang, you must know that I have always loved you, I have dedicated my whole life and soul to you! What? Do you still hate me? Alas, I'm finished... Well, then I'll die for you!" As she said, she pointed the gun at her head and fired. At this time, Yu Guang was too late to regret. He hurried forward, picked up Ye Qiuxin, and saw Ye Qiuxin in gasping breaths, took out a silk hat from her close-fitting shirt, and said to Yu Guang: "This is your,

your hat, I don't know how many millions of times I have kissed it, now I'll give it back to you!" Yu Guang was stunned. "There's my blood on it, blood shed for love!" Yu Guang was moved to tears. Yu Guang! Don't be sad, listen to my tears, you have forgiven me, sympathized with me, I am very satisfied... Yu Guang: Don't cry, this is the sweetest time of my life, I am very happy!" Ye Qiuxin said intermittently, and those weak eyes stared at Yu Guang's face that was shedding tears, "You... before my breathing stops, please give me a kiss. This is my last request..." In this way, in Yu Guang's arms, in Yu Guang's last kiss, Ye Qiuxin slowly died!

This is the last scene of Qiu Qixiang's "The Fire of Youth". It is really passionate and tense! In fact, this is all the "Fire of Youth" at work! (Yet酬)

Letter to the Editor 343

After reading the film special of your newspaper on December 3rd, it contained a message about the establishment of the Modern Film Research Association, which was initiated by Dong Xiangping and others. In addition to being an actor in the Star Film Company, I have not participated in any organization. I have not heard of the organization of this Modern Film Research Association. Perhaps the name is the same, and there is someone else. I am afraid of misunderstandings, so I hereby declare that I hope you will publish this letter in the special column. Dong Xiangping respectfully. December 5th.

Film Novel *Little Women* (Part 2) 344

— Su Yin

The five women, each carrying a box, went out of the March house in single file. In the house across the street, a child was looking out the window. Qiao said: "I think the child in the Lawrence house is pitiful. He came home from Europe from afar, and was locked in an empty house by that old monster who is his grandfather." As she spoke, she couldn't help waving to him. Meg forbade her and said, "Don't do that. People will think you are waving to greet him." Qiao was very stubborn and waved even more vigorously. She thought the child could not see her. But she accidentally looked back and saw that he was also waving. She blushed and rushed ahead with Ya Mei. She thought to herself: "(That child is very cute. I want to get to know him. But Meg's expression is very serious. I will always think of a way..." She had already made up her mind.

The child from the Lawrence house watched the Christmas parade go by from the window upstairs in his own house. He often spied on them from the window. He also knew their names, because he heard them when they called each other. He guessed that Meg was the oldest, probably one or two years older than himself. She was a sweet, kind, and quiet girl, and he knew that she had to walk across the small mountain every day to teach the children of the Jin family in that big house. He hoped that the children of the Jin family would not be as naughty as himself, so that Meg would not be too uncomfortable, because his own teacher, John Brooke, was often bullied by him. Brooke's age was not much older than Meg's. It wasn't that he didn't like Brooke, but he always liked to make fun of him somehow. He thought Qiao was about the same age as him. She was like a boy, and she was probably the most naughty of the sisters. She had to go to her aunt's house every day to be the companion of that old pervert aunt. That was certainly not a good job, so as soon as she returned to her own house, she jumped and was free like a horse without a bridle. But sometimes, she also wrote things in the small room upstairs, frowning as if she was thinking deeply, but I don't know what she was writing. Bess was the shyest, the child from the Lawrence house thought, but she was the sweetest. Everyone in the family looked up to her the most. Sometimes, when Qiao and Ya Mei argued, Bess always acted as a mediator. Ya Mei was still a little sister. She had the longest golden curls, just like a princess in a story. She liked to pretend, liked elegance, and liked to use very long words, he thought of this and smiled.

He was still looking out, not knowing where they were going when they each took something during breakfast. He looked out the window and saw that the things on their table were gone, and he also saw their maid Hannah seem to be wiping her tears, putting a basin of bread and a can of milk on the table. Oh! They must have taken the Christmas breakfast to help the poor! People like them like to do that kind of good deeds!... The March family is very poor, but they can still give some to those who are even less served than them. He thought to himself, wanting to help them too. So he sneaked into his grandfather's study. (To be continued)
